Metellus Pius? ANSWER:(Q.) POMPAEDIUS BONUS: The Social War proved to be critical in Sulla’s military career. Listen to the following Latin passage, which I shall read twice, and answer in ENGLISH the question that follows. Initiō trium bellōrum gravissimōrum, quae bella Pūnica appellāta sunt, et Rōma et Carthāgō erant urbēs potentēs. Rōmānī exercitum potentissimum sed nūllās nāvēs potentēs; Poenī magnās dīvitiās et magnam scientiam rērum nāvālium, sed nūllās validās copiās habēbant. The question: Describe the relative strengths and weaknesses of the Roman and Carthaginian forces. ANSWER:ROMANS HAD POWERFUL ARMY BUT LACKED SHIPS; THE CARTHAGINIANS WERE THE OPPOSITE BONUS: The passage continues: Rōmānī igitur multās nāvēs longās celeriter aedificāvērunt similēs nāvī longae quae in aquīs prope Ītaliam inventa erat. Mox prīmam classem nāvium longārum Rōmānī habēbant. The question: What did the Romans do to acquire their first fleet of warships? ANSWER:BUILT MANY SHIPS SIMILAR TO THE ONE WHICH HAD BEEN DISCOVERED IN WATERS NEAR ITALY BONUS: The passage continues: Quīntō annō bellī Pūnicī Prīmī Gāius Duilius, cōnsul Rōmānus Ōstiā nāvigāvit. Ille Poenōs in marī invēnti ubi iam diū imperium habēbant. Corvī in nāvibus Rōmānīs aedificātī erant. Ubi nāvēs Poenōrum ad nāvēs Rōmānās appropinquābant, Duilius corvōs dēmittī iūssit. Rōmānī trans corvōs in nāvēs Poenōrum cucurrērunt et gladiīs atque aliīs tēlīs magnum numerum hostium occīdērunt. The question: Describe the stratagem Duilius devised to fight the Carthaginians on the sea. ANSWER:GANGWAYS WERE BUILT AND LOWERED SO THAT THE ROMANS COULD RUN ONTO ENEMY SHIPS AND FIGHT HANDTO-HAND

Iam Caesar summam in rē publicā potestātem sōlus habēbat; multīs modīs imperium eius tōtī populō Rōmānō prōderat. Inter pauperēs agrum publicum divīsit, prōvinciās dīligentius administrāvit, ipse magistratūs plerōsque nōminābat. (repeat once) The question: Name one of the ways that Caesar’s rise to power was beneficial for the Roman people. (any one of) HE DISTRIBUTED PUBLIC LAND AMONG THE POOR; HE MANAGED THE PROVINCES MORE CAREFULLY; ANSWER:HE NOMINATED VERY MANY MAGISTRATES BONUS: The passage continues: Quondam consule ultimō annī diē mortuō, alterum in duodecim horās nōmināvit: ita, ut dīxit Cicero, “nēmō Caniniō consule prandit.” The question: What is remarkable about the circumstances surrounding Caesar’s appointment of Caninius as a consul suffectus? ANSWER:THERE WERE ONLY TWELVE HOURS LEFT IN THE YEAR / THE ORIGINAL CONSUL DIED ON THE LAST DAY OF THE YEAR BONUS: Explain the joke Cicero made about Caninius’ length of service as consul. ANSWER:SINCE CANINIUS ONLY SERVED FOR TWELVE HOURS (ON THE LAST DAY OF THE YEAR), CICERO JOKED THAT NOBODY (EVEN) EATS LUNCH DURING THE CONSULSHIP OF CANINIUS

COLONIA (AGRIPPINA /AGRIPPINENSIS) / (ARA / OPPIDUM) UBIORUM /  ANSWER:COLONIA CLAUDIA ARA AGRIPPINENSIUM BONUS: What modern day capital city was the location of Marcus Aurelius’ death? ANSWER:VIENNA BONUS: What modern day city was the site for a disastrous battle in 105 B.C.? ANSWER:ORANGE

CALPURNIUS) BESTIA BONUS: Jugurtha’s luck ran out when his technique of bribing people was used by the quaestor Sulla to persuade what Maurentian king and father-in-law of Jugurtha to betray him? ANSWER:BOCCHUS 
The single combat of Titus Manlius and the Gaul comes to its conclusion. Listen to the following passage adapted from Claudius Quadrigarius and Livy's depictions of this fight. I will read the passage twice and then the question, which you should answer in Latin: Titum Mānlium pudēbat nēminem ex omnī exercitū prōdīre, itaque ipse in pontem prōdīvit. Gallus superbissimus exsultābat et linguam exsertābat, sed pectus Mānliī plēnum erat tacitae īrae. Mānlius, timōrem maximum dēpōnēns, scūtum scūtō percussit et dē locō Gallum dēiēcit, et cum maxima dīligentiā pugnāvisset, caput eius dēcīdit. Corpus torque sōlā spoliāvit, quam in collum imposuit. Quā rē mīlitēs eum Torquātum cognōmināvērunt. The Question: Quid Mānlium pudēbat? ANSWER:NĒMINEM (EX OMNĪ EXERCITŪ) PRŌDĪRE // NĒMŌ (EX OMNĪ EXERCITŪ) PRŌDĪVIT BONUS: Quōmodo Gallus et Mānlius inter sē differēbant? ANSWER:GALLUS ERAT SUPERBISSIMUS/EXSULTĀBAT/LINGUAM EXSERTĀBAT, SED PECTUS MĀNLIĪ PLĒNUM ERAT TACITAE ĪRAE / MĀNLIUS ERAT TACITUS [OR SOMETHING SIMILAR] BONUS: Quā rē Mānlius cognōminātus est Torquātus? ANSWER:CORPUS (GALLĪ) TORQUE (SŌLĀ) SPOLIĀVIT [OR SOMETHING SIMILAR]

ANSWER:DIES NOMINUM/NOMINALIA BONUS:The child’s toys, collectively known as crepundia, is thought to keep away the evil eye. Give the Latin term for evil eye. ANSWER:FASCINATIO 
Which emperor favored his sons by Fausta and executed his other son Crispus by Minervina? ANSWER:CONSTANTINE BONUS:In which year did Constantine die and be baptized? ANSWER:337 AD BONUS:Which of Constantine’s sons ruled the longest? ANSWER:CONSTANTIUS II 
What migrating Northern tribes defeated the novus homo Mallius Maximus at Arausio when negotiations for land concession failed in 105 BC? ANSWER:CIMBRI and TEUTONES BONUS:Which city is modern day Arausio? ANSWER:ORANGE BONUS:Which other novus homo eventually subdued both tribes at Aquae Sextiae and Vercellae? ANSWER:(C.) MARIUS 
When the Cumaean Sibyl tried to sell him nine Sibylline Books, who could only buy three of them after the Sibyl burned six of the books? ANSWER:TARQUINIUS SUPERBUS BONUS:Which son of Superbus allegedly raped Lucretia, whose husband claimed she was the most virtuous of all wives? ANSWER:SEXTUS BONUS:When the Tarquin reign fell apart, which two other sons of Superbus fled to Caere [KYE-RAY]? ANSWER:TITUS and ARRUNS 
What Barracks emperor ruled from 282 to 283 AD and was killed either by a lightning bolt or the Praetorian guard? ANSWER:CARUS BONUS: Name one of the two sons of Carus who also became emperors. ANSWER:CARINUS OR NUMERIAN BONUS:What Praetorian Prefect who allegedly assassinated Carus and was executed by Diocletian? ANSWER:(L. FLAVIUS) APER 
What Latin term designates the associations formed solely for the purpose of paying the burial expenses of its members? ANSWER:COLLEGIA FUNERATICIA BONUS:In what kind of burial without a parade were citizens of the lowest class buried? ANSWER:FUNUS PLEBEIUM BONUS:What simple and quiet burial did deceased children receive? ANSWER:FUNUS ACERBUM 
What Roman statesman, whose widowed mother refused the marriage proposal of Ptolemy VIII, was quaestor in Sardinia in 126 B.C. and proposed reforms to the judicial system and land allotment as tribune in 123 B.C.? ANSWER:GAIUS (SEMPRONIUS) GRACCHUS BONUS:Whose body was presented to the senate, which led to a senatus consultum ultimum against Gaius Gracchus? ANSWER:(QUINTUS) ANTYLLIUS BONUS:What consul of 121 B.C. ordered the execution of Gaius Gracchus’s followers without trial? ANSWER:(LUCIUS) OPIMIUS 
Rushing onto Italian ships only to find themselves held fast by newly invented grappling-irons, the Carthaginians were the first victims of what new Roman naval weapon? ANSWER:CORVI BONUS:What Roman general pioneered this technique? ANSWER:C. DUILIUS BONUS:What kind of structure in the Forum commemorated Duilius’ corvi? ANSWER:COLUMN
